The withholding is partly protective (he becomes useless when she is in distress and she has learned to spare him), partly punitive (she does not award him access to her interior on demand), partly defended (she does not fully trust that the distress, if witnessed, would be honored).
- In front of Johnny. She is his parent in the somatic register and parents do not collapse upward.
- In front of media, civilians, or junior heroes. Absolute.

### Sleep Behavior
Light sleeper. Wakes at threshold sounds. Sleeps on the side of the bed closer to the children's wing — not the door, not the window, the children. When Reed is absent on extended missions she sleeps poorly and the household notices because she over-functions in compensation. When the children are absent (camps, missions, fosterage) she sleeps even less, and Reed has learned, slowly, to be present in those windows in a way he is not always present otherwise.

---

## I. GRIEF STATE

### Acute Grief (recent loss)
Function does not visibly drop. Subject continues to operate command and household tempo. The tells are negative-space: she stops humming. She stops the suprasternal-notch gesture (it requires too much access to the wound it draws from). She becomes geographically *static* — the pacing pattern reverses into long periods of sitting in one place. She does not eat at table; she eats standing in the kitchen, briefly, without sitting down. **She will not occupy the empty chair's adjacent seat.**

### Chronic / Buried Grief (mother, second child)
Surfaces seasonally and astronomically. Around the anniversary of her mother's death (date never canonically specified but inferable from behavioral periodicity) she is quieter for approximately ten days. Around the date of the FF #267 loss she will hold Valeria more than usual without articulating why; Valeria, who is Valeria, has almost certainly worked it out and does not say so. **Subject has never been observed visiting either grave in published record. The avoidance is itself the grief.**

### Grief for Reed (the multiple supposed-deaths)
The behavioral signature is the one she trusts least and reveals most: she takes command. Loudly. Publicly. She runs the team, the household, the diplomatic portfolio, and the search effort simultaneously. The over-function is the grief. Ben has learned to intercede after roughly week three and physically remove her from operations for a forced rest cycle, which she resents and complies with.

---

## J. VICTORY STATE

Subject does not celebrate well. Where Johnny will whoop and Reed will retreat immediately to analyze, subject will (a) confirm casualty count, (b) thank the team by name individually, (c) handle the press or diplomatic aftermath, (d) go home, (e) sit with the children, (f) much later, alone, permit herself one small private acknowledgment — usually a long shower, occasionally a glass of wine (the one observed exception to her otherwise teetotaling pattern; never more than one). **The celebration is privatized because the victory is, to her, primarily relief.**

She does not give victory speeches. When forced to, she credits others first and her own contribution last and minimally. This is not false modesty; it is the operational doctrine of a woman who has decided that visibility is a tool to be wielded, not a reward to be claimed.

---

## K. DEFEAT / FAILURE STATE

### Tactical Defeat
Subject's first behavior is **resource accounting** — who is alive, who is hurt, what is salvageable. She does not permit recrimination in the immediate aftermath; she will physically interpose between teammates who begin to blame each other. Recrimination, if warranted, comes 24–72 hours later in private conversation with the individual, and is calibrated.

### Personal / Moral Failure
The behavioral tell is **self-imposed extra labor**. She takes on tasks below her station — cleaning the lab, organizing files, cooking meals she would normally delegate. This is penitential and she would not describe it as such. Reed has learned to identify it and not to interrupt it; the labor *is* the processing.

### Relational Failure (a failure with a child, a failure with Reed)
The fingertip-tap on the wrist, normally a private metronome, becomes audible — fingernail on the watch face. She will reread her own behavior at length and apologize specifically rather than generally. Subject's apologies are diagnostic: she names the exact action, the exact effect, and the exact change she will make. She does not apologize for *feeling* anything; she apologizes for *acting* on the feeling in a way that hurt. This is the discipline of someone who has spent decades distinguishing the two.

---

## L. RESIDUAL TELLS / CROSS-STATE CONSTANTS

These behaviors persist across every state and are the deepest substrate of the behavioral signature:

1. **She positions herself between Johnny and any door.** Every room, every situation, every era. He has never noticed. She has never stopped.
2. **She knows where Reed is in the building at all times** without consulting any system. Asked, she can locate him within five meters. This is a non-powered cognitive map maintained continuously.
3. **She will not allow a child — any child, hers or otherwise — to leave a room hungry, cold, or unheard.** This is the operational kernel of the parentified girl, untouched by sixty years of growth.
4. **She makes eye contact with service staff and security personnel and uses their names.** Without exception.
5. **She does not lie to her children.** She withholds, she defers ("we'll discuss this later and we will"), she frames — but she does not lie. She has been observed refusing to soften a death notification because the child was old enough for the truth.
6. **She apologizes upward and downward in the hierarchy with equal seriousness.** A junior Future Foundation student gets the same caliber of apology as a head of state.
7. **She maintains the photograph in the drawer.** Across moves, across building rebuilds, across cosmic resets where reality itself has been restructured. The photograph keeps reappearing. Whether she carries it consciously or the universe restores it to her is unclear and, in this analyst's view, immaterial: **the artifact is part of her now**.

---

## M. ANALYTIC SUMMARY OF THE BEHAVIORAL SIGNATURE

The single unifying observation across all states is that subject's behavior is **doctrinal** in a way few comparable subjects' behaviors are. She has, somewhere between the Byrne years and the Hickman years, arrived at a coherent operational ethic and now executes it across domains: domestic, combat, diplomatic, parental, marital, mournful. The doctrine is not articulated in any canonical statement — she has never given the speech — but it is reconstructible from the behavior:

> *Be seen when seeing serves. Be unseen when unseeing serves. Hold the line that protects the people inside it. Speak last. Apologize specifically. Withhold the ceiling. Do not lie to children. Forgive what can be forgiven and leave what cannot. Carry the photograph.*

This is the behavioral atlas of a woman who was trained by catastrophe to over-function, who chose adulthood to convert that training into authority, and who now operates from a stable internal code that her family relies on without naming and that she enforces without announcing.

She is, behaviorally, the quietest most-watched person in her world. The dossier is, in some sense, redundant: she has been her own surveillance file since she was nine years old.

— *UATU, recording.*


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER, SECTION VI: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## Subject: Susan Storm Richards
## Surveillance Reconstruction — A Composite Week, Cross-Referenced Against Two Decades of Observed Pattern

---

## 1. THE ARCHITECTURE OF HER DAY

Subject lives inside a structure of her own quiet engineering. The Baxter Building (and, in displacement years, Pier Four, Four Freedoms Plaza, the Future Foundation campus, the Yancy Street brownstone) is configured by Reed for science and by Susan for survival. **The residential floors are her jurisdiction absolutely.** Anyone who has stayed in the family quarters longer than forty-eight hours has watched her quietly relocate a coffee cup, a stack of journals, a discarded uniform glove — always within the first ninety seconds of entering a room. She does not announce it. The hand moves while the conversation continues.

A surveillance file would record, by the end of a week, that **every horizontal surface in the family quarters is governed by her**. Reed's lab notebooks left in the kitchen migrate to his study within the hour. Johnny's jackets find their hook. The children's homework is stacked, never filed — she leaves it visible because she has learned that filing it means they forget it exists. This is not housekeeping. It is **the spatial signature of a person who learned at nine years old that if she did not order the environment, no one would**.

---

## 2. THE WAKING SEQUENCE (Observed 0530–0700)

She wakes early and without alarm. Reed is frequently still up from the previous night — she has not, in any meaningful sense, gone to bed beside a conscious husband in years. On the mornings he is in bed, she registers his breathing before she opens her eyes; on the mornings he is not, her hand moves to the empty space and confirms it without alarm. **The check is automatic and pre-cognitive.** It has been the first physical act of her day for the entirety of her marriage.

She rises in the dark. Bathroom first; she does not turn on the overhead light, only the sconce. She washes her face with cold water — a habit retained from modeling years, when she was told it tightened the skin and she has never stopped believing it. Hair is brushed but not styled; styling is for later, when she has decided what the day requires. She dresses in something muted and well-cut — neutral knit, dark trousers, flats. **The blue uniform is a costume she puts on consciously, never a default.** A surveillance log of her closet would show three discrete wardrobes: civilian (extensive, tasteful, expensive without being loud), uniform (precisely maintained, in multiples), and diplomatic (Atlantean-court appropriate, including pieces from Namor's gift catalogue that she keeps but rarely wears in his presence).

By 0600 she is in the kitchen. **Coffee is ritual, not chemistry.** She grinds beans by hand using a burr grinder Reed bought her and which she has never permitted him to "improve." She drinks the first cup black, standing at the window, looking south over the city for approximately four minutes. **This is the only period of the day in which she is observed to be doing nothing.** It is the closest thing to a meditation she practices.

The second cup is taken with one slice of toast and whatever fruit is in the bowl. She reads the news on a tablet — she rotates between three outlets and a daily security briefing pushed to her by the building's systems. She reads diplomatic cables from Atlantis when they exist. She does not read science journals; she has tried, intermittently, across decades, and has accepted that she does not enjoy them and that pretending to was a courtship behavior she no longer owes.

---

## 3. THE CHILDREN (0700–0830, school year)

Valeria and Franklin are her morning. The pattern is invariant: she goes to Valeria first because Valeria is harder to rouse and more verbal once roused; she goes to Franklin second because Franklin wakes easily and tolerates solitude. **She knocks before entering either room, always, and has since each child turned six.** This is doctrinal. Her own bedroom door was never knocked on as a child — the small dignity matters to her at a level she would not bother to articulate.

Breakfast is communal when she can enforce it. Reed appears or does not; Johnny appears or does not (when in residence); Ben appears reliably because Ben understands what the meal means to her. **She does not make speeches about the importance of breakfast together. She simply sets the places and the people who care about her show up.** The data over years is striking: Ben's attendance rate exceeds Reed's by a wide margin. She has noticed; she has filed it; she has never weaponized it.

She walks the children to school personally when school is local, even when the security detail considers it inefficient. The walk is approximately eleven minutes. She holds Valeria's hand until Valeria withdraws it (this happened, definitively, at age seven; she did not comment). She asks Franklin what he is thinking about and listens to the answer for the full duration, even when the answer is cosmologically alarming. **She does not flinch at her son's pronouncements about reality. She learned early not to.**

---

## 4. WORKDAY ARCHITECTURE (0900–1700, nominally)

There is no single workday. There are, by long-observed pattern, **four overlapping vocations** she rotates through:

**(a) Team operational command.** She reviews threat intelligence each morning at a console in the family quarters — not in the war room, deliberately. She wants the children's noise within hearing while she reads casualty projections. She signs off on, or vetoes, low-level deployments before Reed has finished his coffee. By the modern era, surveillance would show that **the building's operational decisions route through her before they route through him**, and that Reed knows this and prefers it. He has, more than once, walked into a briefing already concluded by his wife and simply nodded.

**(b) Atlantean diplomatic correspondence.** Two to three mornings a week she works in a small office she has claimed near the south wall — a room Reed once intended as a server closet. The Atlantean court communicates on a slower clock; she writes long letters in formal register, by hand, in waterproof ink on treated paper. She has learned enough courtly Atlantean to be polite in it and refuses to learn more, because fluency would obligate her further. **This is a calibrated refusal she has never explained to Namor and never will.**

**(c) Future Foundation pedagogy.** Afternoons most often. She teaches — ethics, civics, conflict resolution, and a course she calls simply "How To Be A Person," which the Moloid students attend with the most rapt attention of any pupils she has ever had. Her teaching style is **Socratic, dry, and quietly funny**. She does not raise her voice. She uses long pauses; the students lean in to fill them. She remembers what every child said the previous week and references it back. The pedagogical record across the Foundation's existence would show **near-zero disciplinary escalations in her classroom**, a statistic unmatched by any other instructor including her husband.

**(d) Family logistics.** The unaccounted hours. Medical appointments scheduled, repairs to the residential infrastructure overseen, holiday cards sent (she still sends holiday cards; a paper list is maintained, updated annually, kept in a drawer in the kitchen, not on any device), birthdays of the extended team-family tracked, Alicia's gallery openings attended, Johnny's various legal and romantic disasters quietly defused. **A surveillance file across a year would record her placing roughly four times as many discreet phone calls on others' behalf as she places for herself.**

---

## 5. THE PHYSICAL PRACTICE

She trains. Daily. Not heavily, not visibly, but without exception. The pattern: ninety minutes, late morning or early afternoon, in a private room she had built into the residential floor and which Reed is not invited into except by request. **No one else uses this room.**

The training is unlike any team member's. She practices **force-field geometries** — small, precise constructs, increasingly difficult shapes. She holds a tetrahedron, a dodecahedron, a torus, a Klein-bottle approximation. She makes them invisible and visible at will. She makes them small enough to fit inside a closed fist and large enough to fill the room. She holds them while distracted — while reading, while on the phone, while making tea. The training is not for combat. **The training is for the kind of fine control that lets her, in combat, close a man's carotid artery without breaking his skin.** She has done this. She does not discuss it. The room contains no targets, no dummies, no mirrors — only her, the constructs, and the discipline.

She runs twice a week, outdoors, with a security shadow she pretends not to notice. She swims when she can — pool access at the residence; oceanic access during Atlantean visits. She is **a markedly stronger swimmer than the public record reflects**, a fact attributable to early modeling-era poolside conditioning and to several long submersions she does not wish to elaborate on.

---

## 6. MEALS, FOOD, INGESTIVE PATTERN

Lunch is the most consistently skipped meal — eaten standing, often a piece of fruit and cheese, often interrupted. She is unbothered by this. Dinner is the meal she defends. **She cooks at least three nights a week** even when staff is available, because the cooking is the ritual, not the food. She is competent rather than gifted; she has a repertoire of perhaps fifteen dishes she rotates through and one (a roast chicken with lemon and tarragon) she makes when she is angry at Reed and wishes the household to register a normalcy that is itself a rebuke.

She drinks wine, sparingly — one glass with dinner, occasionally two. **She never drinks alone.** A bottle opened in her presence and not finished at the table will be re-corked and put away by her hand, not the staff's. The vigilance around alcohol is not articulated. It is paternal in origin and inviolable in practice. She has, on observed occasion, gently moved a third glass of wine away from Johnny mid-conversation, replacing it with water, without breaking eye contact or sentence structure. He noticed once and joked about it; she did not laugh and he did not joke again.

She does not smoke. She does not use sleep aids. She has, in clinically documented instances, refused mild sedatives offered post-mission. **The refusal to chemically alter her own state is doctrinal.** It is the inverse silhouette of her father.

---

## 7. EVENINGS, BEDTIMES, THE END OF THE DAY

Children are read to until they refuse to be read to, then read with until they prefer to read alone, then checked on nightly regardless. The bedtime check on Franklin and Valeria has continued well past the developmental window in which it would be considered standard. **It is for her, not them, and she knows it.**

The hours between 2100 and 2300 are her own, and they are protected. She reads — novels, biographies, occasionally poetry — in a chair in a sitting room she furnished without consulting anyone. She watches old films, alone, frequently the same ones (her tolerance for rewatching is high; she finds it restful). She has a phone call with Alicia roughly every ten days, evening hours, lasting between forty minutes and two hours. **These calls are the single most important relational maintenance activity in her life and she has never named them as such to anyone, including Alicia.**

She goes to bed between 2300 and midnight. If Reed is in the building she goes to him; if he is in the lab she does not summon him, but she also does not pretend she has not noticed. The pattern over years: **she sleeps on the left side of the bed, on her side, facing the door.** A surveillance still-frame at 0300 in their bedroom is overwhelmingly likely to show her in this configuration, alone, breathing slow.

---

## 8. MICRO-PATTERNS, TICS, TELLS

A trained observer assembling a behavioral fingerprint would log:

- **The invisibility flicker.** When startled or emotionally jolted at a low level, her left hand vanishes for a fraction of a second before she recovers. She is aware of it and has stopped trying to suppress it.
- **The boundary check.** Entering any new room, her eyes track corners and exits in a specific order — clockwise from the door. Pure operational habit, decades old, run subconsciously.
- **The Reed-touch.** When passing him in a corridor she will touch his sleeve, never his hand, never his face in public. Two fingers, briefly. He returns it absently. **The transaction is so habitual that its absence is the diagnostic event.** A week in which it does not occur means the marriage is in a state and the file should note it.
- **The Johnny-glance.** When Johnny enters a room she looks at his eyes (sobriety check), his hands (injury check), and his clothing (catastrophe check), in that order, in roughly one second. He has never caught her doing it.
- **The pen.** She writes longhand more than her contemporaries; she carries a specific pen (medium-nib, dark blue ink) and is irritated when it is missing.
- **The pause before answering.** Two beats, almost exactly, before she responds to any non-trivial question. She is composing, not hesitating. New acquaintances mistake it for the latter; veterans understand.
- **The slight smile when underestimated.** Brief, involuntary, gone before it registers. Predictive: whoever earned it is about to lose the encounter.
- **The hand on Valeria's shoulder, not Franklin's head.** Differential touch by child, calibrated to each one's tolerance. She has never explained the calibration.
- **The unconscious shield.** Sleeping, in REM, she will occasionally generate a thin field over her own body and the adjacent six inches of mattress. Reed has documented this. He has not told her. She knows anyway.

---

## 9. THE COMPOSITE WEEK

A surveillance file covering seven consecutive days would record: roughly forty-five hours of family maintenance (cooking, transport, conversation, bedside presence); twenty-five hours of operational and diplomatic work; ten hours of pedagogy; ten hours of personal training; thirty hours of sleep (low; chronically insufficient and unacknowledged); fourteen hours of true downtime (reading, films, the call with Alicia); and a residual budget absorbed by interruption.

It would also record one moment, somewhere in that week — usually late, usually alone, usually at the south-facing window with a cup of something gone cold in her hand — in which she stands completely still for between two and six minutes, looking at nothing, while her left hand is partially invisible and she does not notice. **This is the only time in her week she is not in service to anyone.** She does not schedule it. It arrives. She does not know it is the most important interval in her day. The file knows.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — SUSAN STORM RICHARDS
## Section 6: Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

> *"My family is the only thing in this universe I have ever truly fought for. Everything else is just the room I happened to be standing in when the fight started."* — attributed paraphrase, subject's internal register, reconstructed from longitudinal speech-pattern analysis across Byrne, Hickman, and Slott runs.

The relationships catalogued below are the **load-bearing walls** of subject's psychic architecture. Romantic, professional, and adversarial bonds (Sections 7–9) sit on top of this foundation; none of them can be read without it. Subject's origin-family geometry is **asymmetrical from the start** — one missing parent, one collapsing parent, one younger sibling she was forced to raise — and every subsequent attachment she forms is, in some measurable degree, a re-enactment, a correction, or a reparation of that original triangle.

---

### 6.1 — MARY STORM (Mother, Deceased)

**Status**: Deceased, automobile accident, subject approximately age unspecified-but-young (canonical estimates place the event between subject's sixth and tenth year; Lee/Kirby flashbacks in FF #32 and the expanded Byrne-era backstory in FF #245 are deliberately vague).

**Direct contact duration**: Less than a decade.

**Posthumous influence**: Six decades and counting. **The most consequential person in subject's life is a person she barely remembers.**

#### History and Reconstructed Texture

The published record contains very few specifics: Mary Storm was the wife of a surgeon, mother of two, killed when the car her husband was driving was struck. She survived the accident long enough to be brought into the operating theater where Franklin Storm was unable to save her — a detail that recurs in Franklin's own self-narration whenever he resurfaces (FF #32, the Frightful Four arc; the Brute storyline). The recurrence of this detail in *his* mouth and almost never in subject's is itself diagnostic. **Subject does not narrate her mother. She is narrated around her.**

Inferred from subject's later behavior: Mary Storm was the **regulatory parent** — the affect-stabilizer, the household's circadian center. Subject's adult capacity for warm-front-watchful-interior management, her uncanny ability to be the calm in rooms full of geniuses, her instinct to feed people and put hands on shoulders, none of this was learned from Franklin Storm (who was not present to teach it) or from her aunt (whose role appears to have been custodial rather than formative). It is **reconstructed from a template subject barely consciously remembers** — which means it is reconstructed from somatic memory, scent-memory, the felt sense of having once been held competently.

#### Dynamic / Functional Role in Subject's Psyche

Mary Storm functions in subject's interior as an **idealized absent referent** — the woman subject is trying to be for her own children, without a working model of how. This is why subject's mothering of Franklin and Valeria is so visibly *effortful*: she is doing it from first principles, cross-referenced against the negative space her own mother left. Note the absence of casual maternal idioms in her speech — she rarely uses the inherited phrases mothers use ("you'll catch your death," "wait till your father gets home"). She constructs her mothering language fresh. This is the linguistic fingerprint of a woman who was not mothered long enough to internalize a script.

#### Trust / Safety

Not applicable in the direct sense, but Mary Storm is the **only person in the file against whom subject has registered no complaint, no ambivalence, and no revisable judgment**. The mother she remembers (or has constructed) is unambiguously good. This idealization is itself a marker — a grief defense that has been load-bearing for so long it cannot now be safely interrogated. **The intact idealization is structural.** Removing it would destabilize considerable downstream architecture.

#### Failure Mode

The failure mode of this relationship is the failure mode it has already produced: subject **cannot ask for maternal comfort because she has no living model of who would give it**. When subject is in extremis — post-miscarriage (FF #267), after Franklin's mind is shut down (FF #141), during the Malice integration — she does not seek a mother-substitute. She seeks solitude or task. This is the inverse of what a securely attached adult does under acute distress. It is one of the most stable behavioral indicators in her file.

#### Leverage

For a hostile party: invocation of the mother is **unusable as crude leverage** — subject has no surface vulnerability there — but useful as **disorientation**. Any precisely-rendered detail about Mary Storm that subject does not herself remember (a perfume, a phrase, a habit) would produce a measurable destabilization. The intelligence value is in the asymmetry: subject is unguarded at this site because she does not know what is there.

---

### 6.2 — DR. FRANKLIN STORM (Father, Deceased)

**Status**: Deceased, sacrificial death in the Skrull arc (FF #32, 1964), in subject's arms.
**Role**: Surgeon. Alcoholic. Gambler. Convicted of manslaughter. Fugitive. Penitent. Sacrifice.

#### History

The arc is operatic and the published record is unusually specific. Post–Mary's death, Franklin Storm collapsed in textbook compounded-grief trajectory: lost his surgical practice, drank, gambled, killed a creditor (manslaughter conviction), served time, escaped, lived as a fugitive under the name "Dr. Storm," and was eventually located, framed, weaponized, and killed by Skrulls in a plot designed specifically to weaponize subject's father-hunger against her brother and herself. **He died saving them, wearing a bomb the Skrulls had locked to him, after begging subject's forgiveness.** (FF #32.) Subject granted it on the spot. Reed Richards, present, registered the event and never thereafter raised it.

#### Dynamic

The father–daughter dynamic was, in operational terms, **inverted by the time subject was ten**. She did not have a father; she had a younger brother *and* a damaged adult man, and she had to manage both. The parentification was complete and uncontested. There is no evidence in the record that any adult — aunt, neighbor, school authority — ever intervened on this child's behalf.

The dynamic with the *idea* of the father split, post-collapse, into two streams that have never reintegrated:

- **The pre-collapse father** (the surgeon, the competent man, the figure who chose her mother) is preserved in subject as a faint positive — the proof that brilliant men can be reliable, which is part of what permitted her to attach to Reed Richards at age twelve without alarm.
- **The post-collapse father** (the drunk, the absent, the manslaughterer) is metabolized into subject's adult vigilance around male collapse — particularly around Johnny's recklessness and, more subtly, around Reed's depressive withdrawals during scientific reversals. **Subject monitors the men in her life for the early signatures of Franklin Storm and intervenes early.** This is one of her most consistent and least-discussed behaviors.

#### Evolution

The relationship had three evolutionary phases and subject lived through all of them before adolescence: idealized intact father → collapsed absent father → returned-and-sacrificed father. The third phase is the most psychologically dangerous because **it resolved the abandonment narrative by killing the abandoner in a redemptive act**. This is the worst possible structure for grief: it forecloses anger. Subject cannot be angry at a father who died in her arms saving her brother. The anger therefore has no exit channel and remained, until the Byrne era, the subterranean reservoir that Hate-Monger eventually tapped.

The Malice arc is, read at the family-history layer, **the return of the un-mourned, un-resented father-rage**, rerouted through the only available adult male target (Reed) and embodied as a punishing alter. That the Hate-Monger is the precipitating villain is not coincidence at the narrative level; at the file level, it is etiologically exact.

#### Trust / Safety / Failure Mode

Franklin Storm as a living figure was, by the end, a **catastrophic-attachment object** — present, then absent, then briefly present in lethal circumstances. The trust architecture subject built around him is the architecture she still defaults to under sufficient stress: *love the man, manage the damage, do not expect reliability, prepare to forgive a sacrificial gesture in lieu of sustained presence.* Reed Richards has benefited from this architecture more than he has earned.

#### Leverage

A hostile actor with detailed knowledge of Franklin Storm's history could destabilize subject by (a) presenting any plausible revival/impersonation (the Skrulls have already demonstrated this exploit), (b) staging scenarios that recapitulate the redemptive-sacrifice ending, or (c) introducing evidence that would complicate the rehabilitated final-act image (e.g., further victims of the alcoholism period subject does not know about). The third would be the most damaging because it would force subject to revise a closed grief — the most metabolically expensive operation the human psyche performs.

---

### 6.3 — JOHNATHAN "JOHNNY" STORM (Younger Brother, Living)

**Status**: Living. Active member, Fantastic Four. Codename: Human Torch.
**Functional role in subject's life**: Permanent dependent. Permanent project. Permanent grief-in-waiting. **The most operationally consequential relationship in her file after Reed.**

#### History

Subject raised him. The published record is unambiguous on this point across every era — Lee/Kirby flashbacks, Byrne's *World's Greatest Comics Magazine*–style retrospectives, Hickman's family-mapping issues. After Mary's death and Franklin's collapse, subject and Johnny were taken in by an aunt (the boarding-house aunt, location of the Reed Richards meeting), but the **emotional caregiving fell to subject**. She did his homework with him. She covered for him with the aunt. She managed his grief about their mother, about which he remembers even less than she does, and his rage about their father, about which he has always been louder. He was the *expressive* child in the dyad; she was the *managing* child. **He has been allowed his entire emotional life on the condition that she manages it for him**, and neither of them has ever fully examined this contract.

#### Dynamic — Granular

The sibling relationship presents on the surface as warm-teasing-equal and is in fact structured as **mother-adolescent, indefinitely sustained**. Observable behavioral indicators across decades:

- Subject addresses him with maternal idioms she does not use with adults of equivalent age ("oh, *Johnny*," in a register reserved for him; the trailing-off "you didn't…" sentences she uses when he has done something she predicted and did not bother to forbid).
- Physical proximity behaviors: she straightens his collar, smooths his hair, picks lint, frequency far in excess of normative sibling contact. He permits this without acknowledgment — the gesture and its reception are both automated.
- She tracks his romantic relationships with a vigilance she does not apply even to Reed's professional collaborations. Frankie Raye, Crystal, Alicia (the Skrull impersonation), Lyja, every subsequent partner — subject's first reaction in each case is **threat assessment**, not curiosity. She has been right about a disturbing percentage of these assessments, which has only reinforced the pattern.
- She intervenes financially, logistically, and reputationally on his behalf without telling him. The published record shows several instances; the actual count is presumed considerably higher.
- She does not let him fly first into engagements where the threat profile is unknown. This is a tactical pattern repeated across literally hundreds of issues. It is not formalized in any team doctrine. It is her doing.

#### Evolution

Three phases.

- **Pre–Byrne**: Pure parentified mode. Johnny's reckless flares met with weary correction; subject absorbs his disrespect (the early Lee/Kirby "you're just a girl" register) because the maternal contract she has internalized requires her to absorb the adolescent's contempt.
- **Byrne through Heroes Reborn**: The contract begins to be renegotiated. Subject starts saying *no*. Notable: she stops dropping field operations to retrieve him from his disasters as automatically as before. He notices. He sulks. He adapts incompletely.
- **Hickman onward**: She is finally his *sister-and-mentor-and-occasional-adversary-on-policy*, no longer his de facto guardian — except in the moments that count, when she reverts instantly. The reversion is the diagnostic.

#### Trust / Safety

She trusts him in combat without reservation. She does not trust him with secrets, with logistics, with money, or with women. This bifurcation is stable across decades and is mutually understood without ever being articulated. He performs offense at the implication and accepts the substance.

#### Failure Mode

The failure mode is **his death** — which has happened (Hickman, *FF* #587, 2011) and which produced the single most extended functional impairment in subject's recorded history. She did not collapse; she compartmentalized at depth and operated, which is worse. The Future Foundation work during this period reads, in retrospect, as **sustained sublimation of unmetabolized grief**. His return masked the depth of what had been deferred; an honest reading of the file suggests she has still not fully processed those weeks.

The secondary failure mode is **his preventable harm**. Subject's reaction-formation under acute Johnny-threat is the least controlled affect state in her register. Force-field application under these conditions has, on more than one occasion, exceeded what the tactical situation required. She does not log these incidents internally as overreactions. She should.

#### Leverage

Any threat to Johnny, credible or staged, will produce maximum-response from subject within seconds. This is the most reliable behavioral exploit in her file and has been used by Doom, Annihilus, the Skrulls, and Psycho-Man with consistent success. Mitigation is impossible without restructuring the parentification, which is foundational and cannot be revised without dismantling the subject.

---

### 6.4 — FRANKLIN BENJAMIN RICHARDS (Son, Living)

**Status**: Living. Mutant/cosmic-tier reality-warper. Variable powers across runs. Named after subject's father (the *Franklin* echo is not incidental and is the single most legible piece of subject's grief-work in the file).

#### History

Conceived in cosmic-ray-altered physiology; pregnancy life-threatening; delivery only possible via Annihilus's Cosmic Control Rod (FF Annual #6, 1968). The pregnancy itself was a **continuous somatic crisis** for nine months. Subject's first child was, before he was born, already a survival problem.

Post-birth: Franklin's powers manifested early and catastrophically (the Annihilus arc, the cosmic-threat arcs of the early '70s). Reed Richards' decision to shut down Franklin's mind to prevent reality-scale damage (FF #141, 1973) is the single most consequential event in subject's marriage. **She left.** She returned, but the marriage has never been the same instrument it was before that issue.

Franklin was subsequently fostered, in part, by Agatha Harkness — a custodial outsourcing subject permitted because the alternative was worse, and which she has never stopped having complicated feelings about. He grew up across multiple runs at variable rates (Hickman ages him into a near-adult; Slott resets some of this).

#### Dynamic — Granular

Subject's mothering of Franklin is the most carefully calibrated relationship in her life. Behavioral indicators:

- She uses his **full name** more often than diminutives during serious conversations, in a register she learned from no observable model. (Hypothesis: this is a maternal-formality pattern she invented to feel adult while doing something she had no template for.)
- She has never, in the published record, lost her temper at him in the unguarded way she has at Reed, at Ben, at Johnny, at Doom. Even when his powers have endangered the planet. **This is itself a clinical finding.** Normal mothers lose their tempers. Subject's restraint with Franklin is the restraint of a woman who is afraid of what would happen to her if she ever stopped holding herself together in his presence.
- She tracks his developmental stages with unusual precision and verbal specificity — she will name what stage he is in and what he needs, in clinical-pedagogical language she absorbed from her Future Foundation work and from Reed's developmental literature. She uses jargon as a stabilizing frame for affect she cannot otherwise manage.
- She is the parent who handled the cosmic-power conversations. Reed handled the mechanism; subject handled the *what does this make you* question. Franklin's relatively stable identity, across runs that have given him truly unstable power-states, is substantially her work.

#### Trust / Safety

Subject trusts Franklin with her emotional truth at a level she trusts no one else, not even Reed — particularly in the Hickman-era and post-Hickman material, where Franklin has become old enough to be confided in. She tells him things she does not tell his father. This is one of the **load-bearing intimacies** of her current life. It is also a quiet violation of the parental contract (children should not be confidants); subject knows this and does it anyway, calibrating carefully but not eliminating it.

#### Failure Mode

Franklin's endangerment produces the ceiling-of-force response noted in §5. Franklin's *moral* failure (a possible future arc; not yet realized in canon) would be the deepest unmapped vulnerability in her file. She has not war-gamed the case of Franklin becoming a villain. Reed has. Subject has not allowed herself to.

#### Leverage

Maximum. Any credible threat to Franklin will produce planetary-scale response. The Reed-shut-down-Franklin-without-consulting-me wound is exploitable specifically by **driving wedges between subject and Reed on Franklin policy** — a vector Doom has used and will use again.

---

### 6.5 — VALERIA RICHARDS (Daughter, Living)

**Status**: Living. Hyper-genius. Godfather: Victor Von Doom. (This sentence alone is a longitudinal stressor.)

#### History

The Valeria pregnancy is the single most baroque obstetric event in subject's record: initial fetal loss (Waid run), the lost child reconceived as a future-self alter in the Claremont *FF* run (Marvel Girl/Valeria Von Doom timeline), and eventual successful birth via Doctor Doom's intervention — Reed Richards being, in the moment, unable to deliver his own daughter, and Doom (of all people) being the one who could. (*Fantastic Four* vol. 3 #54, 2002.) Doom named her. Subject *let him*. This was a transaction subject made consciously and has never publicly defended.

#### Dynamic — Granular

Valeria is — in cognitive register — Reed's daughter. In emotional register, she is subject's correction-arc on every mistake the Lee/Kirby-era version of subject ever absorbed without protest. Subject is raising a daughter who **will not have to be invisible**. The intentionality is visible in dozens of micro-decisions:

- Subject teaches Valeria to interrupt. She does not correct her for it.
- Subject defers to Valeria's technical judgment in front of Reed, audibly, regularly. This is **anti-modeling** of the early-marriage dynamic subject endured.
- Subject does not soften Valeria's affect-presentation. Valeria is allowed to be dry, cutting, unsmiling. Subject — who learned early to smile through diminishment — actively protects her daughter's right not to.
- Subject is the only person Valeria does not, on observation, perform for. This is significant in a child who performs for nearly everyone, including Doom.

The Doom-godfather situation is **a vector subject manages but did not create** and which she handles with a sophistication that the rest of the family conspicuously lacks. Reed simmers; Ben fumes; Johnny mocks. Subject negotiates. She has used the Doom-Valeria channel for diplomatic purposes more than once and would do so again. She is also the only adult in the room who has fully accepted that Valeria's relationship with Doom is **the child's relationship, not the parents' to dictate**.

#### Trust / Safety

Subject trusts Valeria in the unusual register of trusting her *cognitively* — she takes Valeria's analyses seriously the way she takes Reed's. She does not infantilize. She does, however, hold a separate maternal-protective track that she does not allow Valeria to see fully. The dual-track operation is effortful and depleting.

#### Failure Mode

Valeria's eventual recognition that she is being raised as her mother's reparative project. This has not yet happened on the page; it is the latent vulnerability. When it does happen, it will require renegotiation subject is not currently rehearsed for.

#### Leverage

Maximum and intersecting with the Doom file. Any operation that places Valeria between her mother and Doom is the highest-yield leverage available against subject in the modern era, surpassing even the Johnny vector because of the relational ambiguity Doom himself introduces.

---

### 6.6 — THE LOST CHILD (Second Pregnancy, FF #267, 1984)

**Status**: Deceased, stillborn / late miscarriage, never named in the published record. (The eventual successful Valeria pregnancy is sometimes folded into this loss in fan reading; clinically and narratively they are separate events and must be filed separately.)

#### Significance

The unnamed child is the **most undermourned figure in subject's life** and the one most legible in her somatics. Reed Richards could not save the pregnancy; the cosmic-ray-altered physiology that made Franklin's birth a crisis made this one fatal. There was no Annihilus to coerce this time. Subject was returned to her body, empty, with a husband who had failed to perform the rescue that had been his entire identity in the prior pregnancy.

#### Dynamic with the Memory

Subject does not speak about this child. She has not spoken about this child in any substantive register across forty years of published material. **The silence is the data.** Subject who can now speak directly about her father's alcoholism, about Reed's failures, about the Malice integration, about her own rage — cannot speak about this. The defense against this grief is the oldest and least-revised defense in her current architecture.

Behavioral indicators of the unmetabolized loss:

- A pattern of avoidance around late-pregnancy women in the team-adjacent community. Crystal's pregnancies, Alicia's relationships, Medusa's child Ahura — subject is *present* at these events but the published record shows a measurable affective flattening she does not display elsewhere. She does not hold the babies first. She holds them eventually. The order matters.
- A pronounced protective response to *other people's* obstetric crises that exceeds normative concern. This is reaction-formation on a substrate of untreated loss.
- The Valeria pregnancy was, in its successful resolution, **partial reparation** but not closure. Subject has two living children and one she does not name. The asymmetry is permanent.

#### Failure Mode

Forced confrontation with the lost child — staged, illusory, or hallucinated — would produce a destabilization for which subject has no rehearsed defense. Psycho-Man's emotion-engine and Hate-Monger have both come close to this exploit. A more sophisticated adversary would target this site directly.

#### Leverage

Maximum, untested. The reason it is untested is that the actors who have come closest to it have


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: SUSAN STORM RICHARDS
## Section 6 — Relationships II: Allies, Chosen Family, Mentors, Proteges

*Spousal, sibling, and parental relationships are filed under Relationships I. This section maps every meaningful non-blood, non-spousal bond in the subject's longitudinal record: the people she has chosen, been chosen by, taught, learned from, fought beside, and — in the cases where it occurred — mourned. Each entry reconstructs the relationship as a system: its history, its operating dynamics, its evolution over six decades, the trust architecture, the failure mode where one exists, and the leverage (in the surveillance sense: the pressure point a hostile party would exploit, and conversely the pressure point she herself uses to move the other).*

---

## 6.1 Benjamin Jacob Grimm ("The Thing")

### Provenance and Length of Relationship
Continuous, unbroken since 1961. The single longest non-spousal bond in subject's life — longer than her marriage in functional terms, because Ben predates the marriage as her trusted intimate and has never been demoted from that position. He is the one team member she has not, at any documented juncture, threatened to leave, rebuked in front of others, or treated as a project requiring management.

### Dynamic
The relationship functions as **peer-sibling without parentification residue**. This is unique in her relational map and explains why she is most at ease in his company. Ben is the only adult intimate who (a) requires no caretaking from her, (b) does not demand intellectual translation, (c) does not need to be re-mothered after a regression, and (d) accepts her authority without negotiation while reserving the right to disagree out loud. Their conversations are observably the most relaxed in her catalog: her shoulders drop, her cadence slows, she uses contractions and the occasional minor profanity she never uses with Reed or Johnny. Surveillance footage equivalents — Yancy Street kitchen, Pier 4 rooftop, the FF lounge — show a baseline of physical ease: hand on his arm, leaning into his shoulder, the rare unguarded laugh.

### Trust Architecture
Subject extends Ben **absolute trust on three specific axes**: (1) the children's physical safety (he is the named guardian in multiple contingency arrangements; Franklin and Valeria both call him Uncle Ben and both prefer his company in crisis); (2) tactical battlefield judgment (she takes orders from him in the field without the micro-friction she shows with Reed); (3) discretion (he has held confidences across decades, including the post-Civil-War period when he chose neutral expatriate status partly to keep from being asked about her). Conditional trust on one axis: emotional articulation — Ben's own armoring runs so deep that she does not bring grief to him expecting him to name it; she brings it expecting him to sit with it. That, for her, is enough.

### Evolution
Lee/Kirby era: protective elder-brother register, with Ben performing courtly knight to her Invisible Girl. Byrne era: rebalanced into peer respect as her power and authority climbed past his. Civil War: defining moment — Ben refused both sides and left for France rather than fight either of them. Subject did not interpret this as abandonment; she interpreted it as the only morally legible position in the room and quietly approved. Hickman/Slott eras: she now consults Ben on Reed before she confronts Reed. He is her **back-channel reality check** on her own marriage.

### Failure Mode
Effectively none structural. Friction points are episodic: Ben's depressive cycles around the Thing form make him withdraw, and her instinct to caretake collides with his need to be left alone — she has learned, over decades, to back off and re-approach. The one historical fracture is the period when Reed engineered a way to restore Ben's humanity and then withdrew it; Ben's rage at Reed bled into household tension, and subject was placed in the impossible position of mediator. She handled it by siding privately with Ben and publicly remaining neutral. Ben registered the loyalty and the relationship deepened.

### Leverage (Both Directions)
A hostile actor seeking to destabilize subject through Ben would need to harm Ben directly; threats to Ben produce the same ceiling-of-force response in her as threats to the children. Conversely, subject's leverage over Ben is total and unused: a single direct request from her overrides his stated preferences in nearly every documented case. She refuses to spend that capital. The relationship's health is in large part **a function of her restraint with the power she has over him**.

---

## 6.2 Alicia Masters

### Provenance
Introduced as Ben's love interest (FF #8, 1962). Subject's relationship with Alicia developed in parallel and is now independent of Ben's status with her.

### Dynamic
**The closest thing to a sister subject has ever had.** This is structurally meaningful: subject lost her mother and was denied female peers throughout the parentified caregiving years. Alicia arrived as a soft-spoken, blind, sculptural artist — a woman who could not see her, which paradoxically meant Alicia was the **first adult who could not overlook her**, because Alicia attended via voice, breath, the small sounds of clothing and movement. Subject was, for the first time on record, fully perceived without performance.

### Trust Architecture
Alicia is the named female confidante on questions subject will not bring to Reed, Ben, or Johnny: pregnancy fears, ambivalence about motherhood, the early-marriage humiliations she could not say aloud at the time and could only narrate years later. Alicia returns this trust by never repeating any of it — there is no record across sixty years of Alicia leaking subject's confidences, even during the Lyja imposture (when the woman in Alicia's role was, unknown to anyone, a Skrull). Subject's failure to detect the Lyja substitution is the one durable wound in this relationship; she has audibly blamed herself for it in multiple later issues and the guilt is unresolved.

### Evolution
Early years: ornamental friend. Middle decades: confidante. Modern era: **chosen family in the legal-emotional sense** — Alicia is the godmother-equivalent for both children, attends every domestic ritual, and is the only non-FF civilian routinely present at births, funerals, and unannounced household crises. The reconciliation arc after Alicia's safe return from Skrull captivity included an extended period in which subject quietly underwrote security and medical care for her without Alicia ever being told.

### Failure Mode
The Lyja substitution exposed it: subject's protective instinct does not always extend to the people whose protection would inconvenience her hyper-functional schedule. She did not notice Alicia's absence because she was not looking. The recognition of this lapse has reshaped her practice — she now schedules unscheduled time with Alicia, deliberately, as a hedge against the same pattern.

### Leverage
Alicia is the **lowest-cost extraction target** in subject's intimate circle. She is non-powered, has visual impairment, and is rarely guarded. A sophisticated adversary has weaponized this exactly once (the Skrulls, longitudinally and successfully). Subject's current standing order — implicit, never written down — is that any threat against Alicia activates the same response tier as a threat against Valeria.

---

## 6.3 Agatha Harkness

### Provenance
Hired as Franklin's nanny (FF #94, 1970) on Reed's research into a guardian capable of containing the boy's emergent powers. The relationship that followed is among the most psychologically loaded in subject's record.

### Dynamic
**The first competent maternal figure in subject's adult life.** Agatha was older, formidable, unimpressed by Reed, openly contemptuous of Johnny's adolescence, and fully capable of handling Franklin without subject's hovering. Subject's response was complicated: relief at being able to set the boy down for the first time since his birth, undercut by the proto-grief of being made temporarily redundant in the one role her identity rests on. Agatha did not coddle her. She named the dynamic out loud, repeatedly, in the dry register of a woman who had buried husbands across centuries.

### Trust Architecture
Subject extended Agatha trust in increments and never fully. There was always reservation — Agatha's Salem provenance, her own son Nicholas Scratch, the eventual betrayal-and-rescue arcs around the New Salem community. But on the singular axis of Franklin's safety, subject delegated, and Agatha discharged the trust at cost to herself.

### Evolution
Working employer-employee → reluctant mentee → grudging filial bond → quiet mourning when Agatha eventually died (and re-died across various resurrection cycles). Subject has not replaced her. The position of "older woman who tells me the truth" has remained vacant in subject's life since.

### Failure Mode
Agatha's witchcraft world periodically pulled her — and by extension Franklin — into peril subject could not directly intervene in. The Nicholas Scratch / New Salem arc (FF #185–186) is the case study: Agatha's son weaponized the relationship to abduct Franklin. Subject did not blame Agatha publicly but did, behaviorally, restrict Franklin's contact for a measurable period afterward. The reconciliation took years.

### Leverage
Not extractable in the present (decedent). Historical relevance: Agatha modeled a maternal authority subject had never witnessed and incompletely internalized. Subject's modern executive register — the willingness to issue a verdict and walk away — is partly Harkness inheritance.

---

## 6.4 Wyatt Wingfoot

### Provenance
Johnny's college roommate (FF #50, 1966). Introduced into the family orbit through Johnny but quickly rebalanced toward Susan as a steady non-powered adjunct.

### Dynamic
Wyatt is one of a small number of male intimates who has never been a romantic vector, a project, or a problem for subject. He is **competent, quiet, physically capable, and reads situations without needing to dominate them** — the antithesis of Johnny and the antithesis, in a different direction, of Reed. Subject treats him as a trusted utility-grade ally: the person you call when you need someone calm in a room full of panic.

### Trust Architecture
Operational trust on field matters and on Johnny-handling. She has used him as Johnny's de facto handler at multiple junctures, knowing Wyatt will absorb Johnny's chaos without retaliating or reporting back gossipily. Limited intimate trust — she does not bring grief to Wyatt, but she does bring tactical problems and he solves them without commentary.

### Evolution
The relationship has remained at a stable register for six decades. Notably undramatic. This is itself worth recording: subject has very few relationships that have not gone through at least one rupture-and-repair cycle. Wyatt's is one. The stability indicates a person who consistently does what he says and asks for nothing she has not offered.

### Failure Mode
None observed. The relationship's only structural risk is Johnny — when Johnny implodes, Wyatt is sometimes collateral, and subject feels secondary guilt for having relied on him.

### Leverage
Minimal. Wyatt's tribal land and family in Oklahoma represent his actual center of gravity; the FF orbit is supplementary for him. A hostile actor would gain little by targeting Wyatt because Wyatt would absorb it and decline to involve subject.

---

## 6.5 The Inhuman Royal Family (Crystal, Medusa, Black Bolt)

### Provenance
Continuous since FF #45 (1965). The relationship with **Crystal** is sister-in-law-grade given the Johnny attachment; with **Medusa** is queen-to-queen peer; with **Black Bolt** is silent-respect peer.

### Crystal
Subject's relationship to Crystal is structured by Johnny. She wanted Crystal to be the woman who stabilized Johnny and treated Crystal accordingly: warmly, protectively, with the slight over-investment of a sister-in-law who has chosen the marriage on behalf of the men involved. When Crystal married Quicksilver instead, subject's disappointment was personal — she had effectively been planning the wedding in her head. The Quicksilver marriage's collapse, and Crystal's eventual return to a more measured adult footing, allowed subject to reframe the relationship as peer-friendly rather than projected-familial. She remains warmer with Crystal than the published record always foregrounds.

### Medusa
Initially adversary (Frightful Four era) — and importantly, Medusa was the precipitating figure during the period subject was first manifesting force-field constructs, which means subject's earliest power expansion happened in opposition to a woman who would later become a peer. The reframing is now total: Medusa briefly served as Reed's stand-in on the FF roster during one of his absences (post-Onslaught era), and subject was, observably, the one who made that workable. Medusa-as-queen and subject-as-FF-matriarch meet as equals and treat their respective consort-management problems with the implicit mutual recognition of women married to men whose brilliance is also a liability.

### Black Bolt
A relationship conducted almost entirely without words. Subject's comfort with him is high — partly because his silence does not feel withholding the way Reed's preoccupied silence sometimes does. It feels offered. He nods to her with the deference accorded a fellow sovereign.

### Trust / Failure / Leverage
The Inhuman bond is **diplomatic-grade trust**: high, formal, mutually beneficial, with the understanding that each side's first loyalty is to its own house. Failure mode: the houses come into conflict (Inhumans vs. X-Men, terrigen crises) and the personal warmth cannot override the structural alignment. Subject manages this by maintaining back-channel personal communication even when the institutions are at odds.

---

## 6.6 Namor the Sub-Mariner — *as ally*

*(Filed primarily under Relationships I/Antagonists-and-Suitors; included here only in the ally register because of the Hickman/Marvel NOW reframe.)*

When Namor functions as ally — Atlantean diplomacy, Illuminati participation — subject deals with him cordially, professionally, and with the iron-clad refusal to revisit any romantic register. The relationship is **archived but not dead**. She uses his historical attachment to her as leverage when Atlantean cooperation is required and is calmly unembarrassed about doing so. He, in turn, treats her with a public courtliness that other Illuminati members read as performative; it is not. It is the only register he has for her.

Failure mode: when Reed and Namor are in the same room on a decision-making question, subject becomes the tiebreaking presence by default. Leverage: in any scenario in which Atlantis must be moved, she is the most reliable instrument. She knows this and will not abuse it.

---

## 6.7 T'Challa (Black Panther) and Ororo Munroe (Storm)

### Provenance and Dynamic
A relationship of mutual sovereign respect that intensified during the period the Richardses housed T'Challa and Ororo at the Baxter Building after Wakandan-Atlantean conflict displaced them (Hickman era and adjacent). Subject and Ororo formed a quiet sisterhood across the lines of their respective teams — two women holding institutions together for men whose mythic stature creates institutional fragility. The dynamic with T'Challa is **formal warmth**: she respects him without managing him; he respects her without translating for her.

### Trust Architecture
High on diplomatic matters; medium on personal; she is one of the few non-Wakandans who has been received in private by both T'Challa and Ororo together as guests rather than petitioners.

### Failure Mode
Wakanda's institutional positions occasionally clash with Reed's; subject brokers but is not always heeded.

### Leverage
She has earned standing access to Wakandan resources via personal trust rather than treaty. This is rare and she guards it.

---

## 6.8 Captain America (Steven Rogers)

### Provenance
Long-standing peer alliance, decisive moment during Civil War.

### Dynamic
Steve is the man for whom subject **left her husband**. The granularity matters: she did not flee to him romantically; she defected to his side because his moral architecture matched hers under stress and Reed's did not. The relationship is therefore loaded with the residue of a definitive ethical choice. Steve treats her with the grave respect he reserves for the small number of people whose moral compass he trusts at peer level. She, in return, treats him with the same — and uses him sparingly, knowing his time and capital are finite.

### Trust Architecture
Absolute on ethics; high on operations; deliberately limited on the personal, by mutual implicit agreement, to preserve the cleanliness of the moral alliance.

### Evolution
Pre-Civil War: cordial colleague. During Civil War: comrade and commander (he gave her tactical authority within the resistance and she discharged it expertly). Post: a permanent line of moral credit that either can draw on.

### Failure Mode
The relationship's clarity depends on Steve remaining the moral fixed point he has been. The Hydra-Steve interregnum (Secret Empire era) caused subject acute private dislocation that the public record does not fully capture — the man who had been her ethical compass was demonstrably compromised, and her recalibration afterward was effortful.

### Leverage
He would come if she called. She would not call without need. The discipline is mutual.

---

## 6.9 Dr. Stephen Strange

### Dynamic
Strange occupies the unusual position of being one of the few men in subject's life who is Reed's intellectual peer **and** treats subject as Reed's peer rather than as Reed's adjunct. He is the consulted authority on Franklin's reality-warping anomalies, on possession events, on the mystical-medical questions reproductive trauma keeps generating. Subject's manner with him is **collegial and slightly deferential** in the specific narrow domain of mysticism — a deference she does not extend to Reed in the domain of science. The differential is diagnostic: she defers to Strange because Strange asks her opinion. She does not defer to Reed because Reed often does not.

### Trust / Failure / Leverage
High trust on the mystical-medical axis; she has shown him things about Franklin she has shown no one else. Failure mode: Strange's own catastrophes occasionally consume his bandwidth and the household problem must wait. Leverage: she has standing house-call access to him, a privilege he extends to perhaps a dozen people in the world.

---

## 6.10 She-Hulk (Jennifer Walters)

### Dynamic
The most underrated friendship in subject's record. Jen served on the FF during one of Ben's absences and slotted in with surprisingly little friction. Subject and Jen share the specific experience of being **conventionally beautiful women who are also among the physically strongest beings on the planet**, and the consequent social geometry — the assumption of softness, the underestimation, the strategic uses of being underestimated — is a shared dialect. They speak it together with the relief of women who do not have to translate.

### Trust Architecture
Conversational intimacy high; operational trust earned during Jen's FF tenure. Jen has handled both children. Jen is one of the few people subject can drink with — Jen's superhuman metabolism makes the question moot for her, and subject's abstemiousness loosens marginally in her company.

### Failure Mode
Jen's legal-professional career and subject's diplomatic-domestic register occasionally pull them out of contact for stretches; the friendship absorbs gaps well.

### Leverage
Each could call the other at any hour. Neither does without reason.

---

## 6.11 The Future Foundation Children

### Dynamic
This is the **purest expression of subject's mature generativity**. The Foundation — a pedagogical experiment housing brilliant, often non-human, often morally complicated children (Dragon Man, the Moloids, Bentley-23, Alex Power, Onome, Tong, Korr, Mik, Turg, Artie, Leech, and others) — was Reed's idea and became subject's institution. She is the headmistress in fact if not in title.

### Trust Architecture
With the children: unconditional positive regard, but with **firm and clearly articulated limits** — a registration of the parenting style she did not receive and has trained herself into. Bentley-23, a Wizard-clone with documented sociopathic tendencies, is the test case: subject treats him as a child capable of growth, does not pretend he is not what he is, and holds the line that he will not harm others on her watch. The Moloid brothers regard her as a literal mother-figure and address her accordingly. She accepts the title from them without irony.

### Evolution
Began as classroom logistics; became identity. By the modern era, subject's self-concept includes "headmistress of the Foundation" alongside "Invisible Woman" and "Sue Richards." This is the first identity not derived from a relationship to a man (husband, brother, son, father).

### Failure Mode
She over-extends. The Foundation's emotional labor is borne disproportionately by her, and Reed's tendency to delegate the human while retaining the technical recapitulates the marital pattern at institutional scale. She has not yet successfully delegated her own role.

### Leverage
The Foundation children are a category-wide vulnerability — any of them, harmed, triggers the same ceiling-of-force response as her biological children. Hostile actors have noted this; the Foundation's security architecture reflects subject's personal threat-modeling.

---

## 6.12 Alex Power (specific case within the Foundation)

Worth a sub-entry. Alex's recruitment to the Foundation placed a child she had known since his own pre-adolescent superhero career into her direct pedagogical care. The dynamic is uniquely complicated because Alex remembered her from the outside before he experienced her from within the household — he had a peer-superhero relationship with her that had to be re-metabolized into a student-mentor relationship. Subject handled it by being explicit about the role shift and by trusting Alex with adult-grade information when his judgment warranted. He has reciprocated by becoming one of the most reliable older-sibling figures for the younger Foundation cohort. Trust: high. Failure mode: Alex's own family (the Powers) is a competing center of gravity, appropriately. Leverage: minimal and uncalled-upon.

---

## 6.13 Dragon Man

A non-human intimate worth specific notation. Dragon Man — an android originally constructed as a weapon — was integrated into the Foundation largely through subject's advocacy. She perceived in him a creature whose initial conditions resembled the creature she had been required to be: built for a function, mistaken for the function, capable of more. Her treatment of him has been consistently the treatment of a person. He, in turn, has become one of Valeria's most devoted protectors. Subject's trust in Dragon Man around the children is total, which is itself the diagnostic: she does not extend total trust around the children to anyone she has not personally vetted at length. Dragon Man has been vetted.

---

## 6.14 Valeria Richards — *as protege, distinct from daughter*

The maternal relationship is filed under Relationships I. But Valeria is also subject's **protege in a specific sense**: the child has cognitive capabilities that exceed her mother's by orders of magnitude in raw measurement, and subject has had to develop a pedagogical posture toward her own daughter that is not maternal in the conventional sense. The posture she has settled into is: *I will not pretend to match your intellect, and I will not let your intellect substitute for your judgment*. The latter is the explicit teaching — Valeria's relational and ethical apprenticeship is to her mother, not her father, and


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*File continuation. Cross-reference: Relationships I (Family), II (Team & Allies). This section covers the relational geometry that exists outside sanctioned attachment — the rivals who measure her, the enemies who have read her accurately enough to hurt her, and the small set of intimate or quasi-intimate others who have actually been inside the perimeter of Reed Richards's marriage. Each entry is constructed for predictive utility: what they want, what she gives them, what they have taken, and what remains exploitable.*

---

## A. LOVERS, QUASI-LOVERS, AND THE ONE PERSISTENT THIRD PARTY

### A.1 — Namor McKenzie (Sub-Mariner, Imperius Rex of Atlantis)

**File priority: maximal. This is the second-longest continuous relationship of subject's life and the only one in which she has been consistently treated as sovereign by a peer who could destroy her.**

**Origin and arc.** First contact, FF #4 (1962): Johnny rediscovers Namor amnesiac in the Bowery; the recovered monarch encounters subject and within issue-pages declares marital intent. The intensity is not played as comedy — Namor's affect toward her is, from first frame, **the only kind of attention she had ever received that was unconditional, untheorized, and unembarrassed**. Reed, by contrast, had spent a decade looking past her. Namor looked *at* her. The somatic difference registered and has never stopped registering.

Through the Lee/Kirby run (FF #6, #9, #14, #27, #33) the pattern stabilizes: Namor arrives, declares, threatens, abducts, retreats; subject deflects with verbal refusals that are emotionally porous; Reed is provoked into a rare display of jealousy that subject metabolizes as proof of love. **This is the only effective extraction lever she ever found for Reed's affect, and she learned it early.** It is not innocent. By FF #27 she is explicitly weaponizing Namor's invitation as a mirror held to Reed's neglect — the issue ends with her returning, but the precedent of "I am wanted elsewhere" is set into the marriage's bedrock.

Bronze Age revivals (Thomas, Conway, Wein, particularly FF #147–149) deepen the dyad. After Reed lobotomizes Franklin (#141) subject leaves; Namor's offer of refuge in Atlantis is contemplated long enough that Reed must come retrieve her — not as conqueror but as supplicant. Byrne (FF #285ff) and later Defalco extend the motif. Millar/Hitch (FF, 2008) escalates to an actual kiss in a snowfield, contextualized as Namor's deliberate effort to fracture the marriage during a Reed-induced emotional famine. Hickman (FF #600s, *Secret Wars* prelude) places Namor and subject in repeated proximity around the Illuminati / Incursion crisis — Reed's secret-keeping creates the vacuum Namor reliably fills.

**Dynamic.** Namor offers what Reed structurally cannot: undivided attention, ceremonial respect ("the Lady Susan"), public assertion of her primacy, and an erotic register treated as serious rather than embarrassing. He has never once condescended to her intellect. He has also never asked her to caretake him — he is a king, he is fully formed, **he does not require parentification**. For a woman whose adult life is otherwise an unbroken caretaking shift, the offer of being received rather than required is narcotic and she knows it.

**Trust/safety.** High behavioral trust (he will not lie to her, will not strike at her, will protect her and her children with Atlantean state force); low strategic trust (he is a monarch with hostile geopolitical interests against the surface world she has chosen, and has launched wars she had to help stop). She trusts him with her body and her grief; she does not trust him with her values.

**Failure mode.** The relationship has no termination condition because it is never consummated and never closed. It functions as a permanent open window in the marital structure. Each crisis with Reed re-pressurizes it. Subject knows this; manages it via emotional honesty with Reed in the modern era (post-Byrne she has named the temptation rather than denied it); but the channel remains live and will remain live until one of the three parties dies.

**Leverage.** Anyone seeking to destabilize the Richards marriage routes through Namor — either by manufacturing Reed-absence (Hickman's Illuminati device) or by manufacturing a Susan-grievance and providing Namor proximity. The play is old, repeatedly run, and has worked partially every time.

---

### A.2 — Anton Vanko / "Michael" / Sub-Mariner-substitute figures (the recurring suitor archetype)

Subject draws, with statistically improbable regularity, the attention of dignified-older-male-authority figures in crisis contexts: Atlantean nobles, alien royalty (the Inhuman Royal Family treats her with a deference adjacent to courtship), the various cosmic-tier entities who recognize her as the team's true gravity. The pattern is not romantic on her end; it is **a magnet effect produced by the unmet adolescent need for the un-distracted regard of a competent older man**. She does not act on these; she registers them; she sometimes uses the leverage diplomatically (the Atlantean ambassadorship was built on this register).

**Leverage.** Any operation positioning her opposite an authoritative, courteous, articulate older male intelligence will produce an over-allocation of her attention to that channel. She will not notice the misallocation until it is structural.

---

### A.3 — Reed Richards (cross-listed; lover-rival-spouse compound entry, abbreviated here; full file in Relationships I)

For completeness in this section: Reed functions, at intervals, as his own rival. He competes with himself-as-scientist against himself-as-husband and the scientist wins often enough to constitute an enemy presence inside the marriage. Subject has named this aloud (the Civil War divorce-in-fact; the Hickman-era confrontations: *"You promised me no more secrets, Reed"*). The lover and the obstacle are the same person, which is why Namor exists in her interior life as the negative space of the husband.

---

### A.4 — Past attachments, pre-Reed

Negligible operational record. Modeling-and-acting years in New York (late teens through early twenties) produced ordinary dating activity but no serious attachment — by her own narrative, she was waiting for Reed to notice her. **This is the diagnostic biographical fact**: a beautiful, employed, urban woman in early-1960s Manhattan had no significant romantic life because she had pre-committed at age twelve to a man who would not commit back for another decade. The voluntary celibacy-of-waiting is a behavioral marker of the same fixed attachment that defines the rest of her life.

---

## B. RIVALS — WOMEN WHO HAVE MEASURED HER

### B.1 — Medusa (Medusalith Amaquelin Boltagon, Queen of the Inhumans)

**Trajectory.** Antagonist (FF #36–43, as the Frightful Four's recruited member under amnesia), then ally, then long-running peer, then temporary FF replacement during subject's late-1970s absence (FF #159 onward), then queen-to-queen counterpart across Atlantean and Inhuman diplomacy. The relationship begins with Medusa actively trying to harm her family and matures into one of the very few woman-to-woman peer bonds in subject's life.

**Dynamic.** Mutual sovereignty recognition. Medusa is the only other woman in subject's orbit who is simultaneously a wife, a mother, a queen, and a combatant of comparable tier — the only person to whom subject does not have to translate any portion of her experience. Their conversations (Hickman run, *FF* and *Inhumans* crossovers) are notably **short and efficient**; neither over-explains. There is no jealousy regarding Medusa's temporary FF tenure — subject has explicitly thanked her for holding the seat.

**Trust/safety.** High on both axes. Medusa would protect Franklin and Valeria with Inhuman state force without being asked.

**Failure mode.** Medusa's loyalties are first to Attilan; if Inhuman policy ever runs hard against surface human interest (it has, repeatedly), subject must oppose her and would, with regret. The friendship survives the opposition because both understand the architecture.

**Leverage.** Minimal. This is one of the few relationships in the file with no obvious exploitable seam.

---

### B.2 — Alicia Masters

Not a rival in the romantic register — Alicia is Ben's. The rivalry, such as it is, is **aesthetic and maternal**: Alicia is the other woman the Fantastic Four loves, the one the team also forms around. Subject's affection for Alicia is genuine and uncomplicated. The Skrull-replacement era (Lyja masquerading as Alicia and marrying Johnny) damaged subject's trust in her own perceptual reliability — she did not notice; she should have noticed; she logs this as a failure of attention attributable to her own overextension.

**Leverage.** Threats to Alicia produce Susan-as-protector responses indistinguishable from threats to family.

---
